## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics
**Analysis**: This task models the rate of change of concentration dA/dt as a function of concentration A and time t, which is the fundamental problem of determining rate laws in chemical kinetics. The presence of both A and t suggests either a non-trivial reaction order or a system where other species' concentrations have been expressed as functions of time.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Zero-order rate law: dA_dt = c0 (constant rate, independent of concentration)
- First-order rate law: dA_dt = c0 * A (radioactive decay, unimolecular decomposition)
- Second-order rate law: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 (bimolecular reaction of single species)
- nth-order rate law: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 (general power-law kinetics)
- Mixed-order rate law: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * A**2 (parallel first and second order pathways)
- Michaelis-Menten type: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A) (enzyme kinetics, saturation kinetics)
- Reversible first-order: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 (forward and reverse reaction with equilibrium)
- Autocatalytic reaction: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 + c2 * t) (product-dependent rate with time-substituted product)
- Time-dependent first-order: dA_dt = c0 * A * exp(c1 * t) (time-varying rate constant, e.g., temperature ramp)
- Coupled kinetics (eliminated species): dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 + c2 * exp(c3 * t)) (rate depending on another species expressed via time)
- Inhibition kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A)**2 (substrate inhibition)
- Polynomial rate with time: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * t (linear time-dependent source/sink term)
- Logistic-type kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 + c2 * A) (autocatalytic with limited resources)
- Power-law with time modulation: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 * t**c2 (empirical rate law with aging effects)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope â†’ Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects â†’ Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay â†’ Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior â†’ Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects â†’ Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- If dA/dt is proportional to A^n, the integer or half-integer value of n indicates the molecularity or reaction order of the elementary step
- A linear relationship between dA/dt and A (passing through origin) indicates first-order kinetics; a nonzero intercept suggests a zero-order contribution or reversible reaction
- If dA/dt depends on both A and t, another reacting species' concentration has likely been substituted using its own integrated rate law (e.g., B(t) = B0*exp(-k*t))
- Rational expressions in A (e.g., A/(c+A)) indicate enzyme-like or surface-catalyzed reactions following Langmuir-Hinshelwood or Michaelis-Menten mechanisms
- Negative values of dA/dt indicate consumption of A (reactant), while positive values indicate production (product or autocatalysis)
- Products of A with exponential functions of t often arise from coupled differential equation systems where one equation has been solved analytically
- If the rate law contains A*(c1 - A) or A*(1 - c0*A), this suggests logistic or autocatalytic behavior with a carrying capacity or stoichiometric constraint
- Fractional powers of A (e.g., A**0.5) may indicate chain reaction mechanisms or diffusion-limited kinetics
